Jamison Brereton

114
Rudra
Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
11 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 10тАУ11
A simple but pleasing hymn, characterized by considerable chaining and intertwining of repeated vocabulary and syntactic structures. The helpful and healing aspects of Rudra are emphasizedтАФthe related words sumat├н тАЬbenevolenceтАЭ and sumn├б тАЬfavorтАЭ occur six times in this eleven-verse hymn. His fearsome and angry side is for the most part downplayed, mentioned in passing in verses 4c and 10a, both beginning тАЬin the distance.тАЭ But RudraтАЩs possible punitive actions are addressed directly in verses 7тАУ8, which contain twelve occurrences of the prohibitive negative m─Б тАЬdonтАЩt!тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Rudra By RVic standards this hymn is almost laughably simple and elementary, very different from KutsaтАЩs usual products.

There is much repetition and chaining of vocabulary in this hymn: kс╣гay├бdv─лra- is prominent at the beg. (1-3, + 10), with v─лra- reprised in 3 and 8. See also ┼Ы├бm 1, 2; a┼Ыy─Бma 2-3; sumat├н 3, 4, 9 + sumn─Бy├бn 3, sumn├б 9, 10; n├н hvay─Бmahe 4-5 [hav─Бmahe 8]; n├бmas─Б 2, 5 + n├бmaс╕е 11; tv├йс╣гam 4-5; kapard├нn- 1, 5; mrс╕Н╠е ├б 2, 6, 10 + mrс╕Н╠е ay├бtama 9; tok├б- t├бnaya- 6, 8; hav├нс╕е 3, hav├нс╣гmant- 8; r─Б╠Бsva 6, 9; pit├бr mar├║t─Бm 6, 9; vrс╣З╠е imahe 4, 9; ─Бr├й 4, 10; ┼Ы├бrma тИЪyam 5, 10). The first 5 vss. are also marked by 1st pl. verbs.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe offer these praises to the mighty Rudra, with the braided hair, the destroyer of heroes, in order that health may be enjoyed by bipeds and quadrupeds, and that all being sin this villag may be (well) nourished and exempt from disease.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rudra; he cause sall to weep (rodayati) at the end of the world; or rut, signifying pain, pain of living, which Rudra drives away (dravayati); or, rut, may mean ‘word or text or the upaniс╣гads of the vedas’ by which he is approached or propitiated (druyate); or, rut, may mean ‘holyor divine speech or wisdom’ which he confers (r─Бti) upon his worshippers; or, rut, may mean ‘darkness’ that which invests of obstructs (runaddhi) all things and which Rudra dissipates (vс╣Ыn─Бti); or, while the gods were engaged in battle with the asuras, Rudra, identified with Agni, came and stole their treasure; after conquering the enemy, the gods searched for the stolen wealth, and recovered it from the thief, who wept (arudat), and Agni was thence called Rudra (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.5.1.1). With braided hair: kapardine, from kaparda, jaс╣н─Б of ┼Ъiva; hence, = jaс╣нilaya. ┼Ъiva is recognized as Rudra; Destroyer of heroes: k┼Ыyad v─лr─Бya, in whom heroes (v─лra) perish (vina┼Ыyanti); or,of whom the imperial (kс╣гayantaс╕е pr─Бptai┼Ыvaryaс╕е) heroed (that is, the Maruts) are the sons

Jamison Brereton

These poetic thoughts do we proffer to Rudra, the powerful one with braided hair who rules over heroes,
so that he will be luck for our two-footed and four-footed, so that
everything in this settlement will be flourishing, free of affliction.

Griffith

To the strong Rudra bring we these our songs of praise, to him the Lord of Heroes with the braided hair,
That it be well with all our cattle and our men, that in this village all be healthy and well-fed.

Geldner

Diese frommen Gedanken tragen wir dem starken Rudra vor, dem M├дnnerbeherrscher mit aufgewundenem Haar, auf da├Я es Zweif├╝├Яlern und Vierf├╝├Яlern wohl ergehe und alle Aufzucht in diesem Dorfe gesund sei.

Grassmann

Dem starken Rudra bringen diese Lieder wir, dem M├дnnerherrscher mit dem aufgewundnen Haar, Dass Heil sei dem, was zwei und was vier F├╝sse hat, und alles bl├╝he unversehrt in diesem Dorf.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBe gracious to us, Rudra; grant us happiness, for we worship the destroyer of heroes with oblations; and, by your directions, Rudra, may we obtain that freedom from disease and exemption from dangers which our progenitor, Manu, bestowed upon us, (having obtained them form the gods).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Be merciful to us, Rudra, and create joy for us. To you who rule over heroes we would do honor with reverence.
Whatever luck and lifetime Father Manu won through sacrifice, that may we attain under your guidance, Rudra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The weak pf. form (─Б)yej├й is anomalous in two regards: it does not agree with the standard weak pf. ─лj- and it produces a bad cadence here. The form is found twice elsewhere in the RV: ─Бyej├й in X.63.7 where Manu is also the subj. and the form is in the same (bad) metrical slot - the two passages seem to be connected - and VI.36.2 with the preverbs ├бnu pr├б and in an acceptable metrical slot. The weak pf.

stem ─лj is not found with preceding preverb. The forms are disc. at length by K├╝mmel (391-92) with ample citation of previous lit. Schindler considers ─лj the older form, to the laryngeal-initial root (PIE*Hia╠п ╟╡) with reduplication *Hi-Hij-╠Б , in contrast to *ia╠п - initial roots, which redupl. *ia╠п -iC. For Schindler the yej forms are metrically driven replacements and serve to avoid the coalescence of the vowel of the preverb + ─лj, esp.

in the cadence. (Neither he nor K├╝mmel seems to recognize that the yej forms produce bad cadences, a problem that undercuts the arguments that both of them use to explain their appearance in this context.) K├╝mmel by contrast questions SchindlerтАЩs posited distinction in redupl. between initial laryngeal roots *Hia╠п C and glide-initial *ia╠п C, since the development of super-weak forms of the type ┼лc├║r to тИЪvac happens to roots without initial laryngeals, only glides. K├╝mmel argues that whether or not the root had a preceding initial laryngeal the redupl. to a *(H)i/╠пu╠пaC root was originally always

*(H)i/╠пua╠п -. The u/i-type redupl. developed by analogy to *(H)ai/╠пuC╠п - roots. Therefore ─лj is an inner-Vedic development, not an archaism per Schindler. Yet - even though he thinks yej shows the older reduplication pattern - he still allows the possibility that itтАЩs a new formation nonetheless. K├╝mmelтАЩs disc. is ultimately indecisive.

As for the metrical problem, Ludwig and Arnold want to emend to *─Бyaj├й, of somewhat dubious morphological provenance. I very tentatively suggest another possibility, that in this preverb-verb combination the underlying form was *─Б (H)i(H)ij-ai, with the i-reduplication becoming a glide between ─Б and the redupl.

syllable, which was then originally short: *─Бyij├й. The drawback to this explanation (or one of them) is that there is no obvious source for the -ej that was substituted at some point in the redaction.

Griffith

Be gracious unto us, O Rudra, bring us joy: thee, Lord of Heroes, thee with reverence will we serve.
Whatever health and strength our father Manu won by sacrifice may we, under thy guidance, gain.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRudra, showerer (of benefits), may we obtain, through our worship of the gods, the favour of you, who are the destroyer of heroes;come to our posterity, purposing to promote their happiness, while we, having our sons in safety, offer you oblations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

May we attain your benevolence though sacrifice to the gods, the benevolence of you who rule over heroes, o reward-granting Rudra.
Bestowing only favor, come roaming toward our clans: possessing heroes who cannot be harmed, we will pour you an oblation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the cognate acc. in juhav─Бma тАж h├бviс╕е.

Griffith

By worship of the Gods may we, O Bounteous One, O Rudra, gain thy grace, Ruler of valiant men.
Come to our families, bringing them bliss: may we, whose heroes are uninjured, bring thee sacred gifts,

Geldner

Wir m├╢chten durch Gottesdienst deine, des M├дnnerbeherrschers, Huld erlangen, o belohnender Rudra. Wohlwollend komme zu unseren Niederlassungen. Mit heilen M├дnnern m├╢chten wir dir Opfer darbringen.

Grassmann

Lass deine Gunst erlangen, gn├дd’ger Rudra, uns, des M├дnnerherrschers durch die G├╢tterhuldigung, Zu unsern H├дusern komme her recht hold gesinnt, lass unverletzt an M├дnnern uns das Opfer weihn.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke for our preservation the illustrious Rudra, the accomplisher of sacrifices, the tortuous, the wise; may he remove far from us his celestial wrath, for we earnestly solicit his favour.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The accomplisher of sacrifice: yaj├▒as─Бdham, i.e. s─Бdhayitaram, he who makes the sacrifice well-desired or perfet: sviс╣гс╣нam or su iс╣гс╣нam; The tortuous: vaс╣Еku, he who goes crookedly

Jamison Brereton

We call down turbulent Rudra for help, the wandering poet who brings the sacrifice to success.
In the distance from us let him shoot his divine anger. It is just his
benevolence we choose.

Jamison Brereton Notes

vaс╣Еk├║- is variously interpreted and etymologized; see EWA s.v. In this passage Geldner takes it as тАШden fliegendenтАЩ with ?, Renou sim. (тАШvolantтАЩ without ?); Witzel Got┼Н refuse to tr., but mention the common gloss тАШkrummтАЩ in their n. Assuming (with most) that it belongs to тИЪva├▒c тАШgo crookedly, meanderтАЩ, I take it here as тАШmeanderingтАЩ ├а тАШwanderingтАЩ, characterizing an itinerant poet. See ─Б╠Бcara in the previous vs. (3c), which suggests such wandering. For a different specialization of the root meaning, see I.51.11.

Griffith

Hither we call for aid the wise, the wanderer, impetuous Rudra, perfecter of sacrifice.
May he repel from us the anger of the Gods: verily we desire his favourable grace.

Geldner

Wir rufen den funkelnden Rudra, den Opferf├╝ller, den fliegenden Seher zur Gnade herab. Weit weg von uns soll er den g├╢ttlichen Zorn senden; seine Gunst nur erbitten wir.

Grassmann

Den pr├дcht’gen Rudra rufen wir zur H├╝lfe her, den raschen Seher, der des Opfers Segner ist, Er treibe weit von uns hinweg der G├╢tter Zorn, vor allem w├╝nschen wir uns seine Huld herbei.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke, from heaven, with reverence, him who has excellent food, who is radiant, and has braided hair, who is brilliant, and is to be ascertained (by sacred study), holding in his hands excellent medicaments; mayhe grant us health, defensive armour, and a (secure) dwelling.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Him who has excellent food: var─Бha, lit. a boar and one who has a hard body, like a boar; this is an abbrieviation of var─Бh─Бra, from vara, good, and ─Бh─Бra, food

Jamison Brereton

We call down with reverence the boar of heaven, flame-red, with braided hair, turbulent in form.
Bearing in his hand desirable healing remedies, he will extend shelter, covering, and protection to us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the rhyming figure ┼Ы├бrma v├бrma chard├нr.

Griffith

Him with the braided hair we call with reverence down, the wild-boar of the sky, the red, the dazzling shape.
May he, his hand filled full of sovran medicines, grant us protection, shelter, and a home secure.

Grassmann

Des Himmels rothen Eber mit geflochtnem Haar, sein funkelnd Aussehn rufen wir in Demuth her; Der in der Hand die sch├╢nsten Arzeneien tr├дgt, er m├╢g’ uns reichen festen Schutz und Schirm und Schild.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThis praise, the sweetest of the sweet, and cause of increase (to the reciter), is addressed to Rudra, the father of the Maruts; immortal Rudra, grant us food sufficient for mortals, and bestow happiness on me, my son, and my grandson.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rudra, the father of the Maruts: ‘After their birth from Diti, under the circumstances told in the Pur─Бс╣Зas (Viс╣гс╣Зu Pur─Бс╣Зa), they were behdl in deep affliction by ┼Ъiva and P─Бrvati as they were passing sportively along; the latter sid to the former, “If you love me, transform these lumps of flesh into boys”. Mahe┼Ыa accordingly made them boys of like form, like age, and similarly accoutered, and gave them to P─Бrvati, as her sons, whence they are called the sons of Rudra.’ Hence, maruts are the sons of Rudra. Another legend: P─Бrvati, hearing the lamentations of Diti, entreated ┼Ъiva to give the shapeless births, forms, telling them not to weep (m─Б rodiс╕е); another, that he actually begot them, in the form of a bull, on Pс╣Ыthiv─л, the earth, as a cow

This speech here is spoken to the father of the MarutsтАФspeech sweeter than sweet, strengthening to Rudra.
Both grant us, immortal one, what nourishes mortals, and be merciful to our selves, to our progeny and posterity.

Griffith

To him the Maruts’ Father is this hymn addressed, to strengthen Rudra’s might, a song more sweet than sweet.
Grant us, Immortal One, the food which mortals eat: be gracious unto me, my seed, my progeny.

рд╣реЗ рд░реБрджреНрд░ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдВ рдорд╛ рд╡рдзреАрдГ рдорд╛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реАрдГ ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН рдЕрд░реНрднрдХрдВ рдмрд╛рд▓рдВ рдорд╛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реАрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдЙрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрдВ рд╕реЗрдХреНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рдордзреНрдпрд╡рдпрд╕реНрдХрдВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рдорд╛ рд╡рдзреАрдГред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН рдЙрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдВ рдЧрд░реНрднрд░реВрдкреЗрдг рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрд╖реБ рдирд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрдордкрддреНрдпрдВ рдорд╛ рд╡рдзреАрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдкрд┐рддрд░рдВ рдЬрдирдХрдВ рдорд╛ рд╡рдзреАрдГред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдорд╛рддрд░рдВ рдЬрдирдиреАрдВ рдорд╛ рд╡рдзреАрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдиреЗрд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдГ рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рддрдиреВрд╖реБ рднрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╣реЗ рд░реБрджреНрд░ рдорд╛ рд░рд┐рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ рдорд╛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реАрдГ рее рд╡рдзреАрдГ ред рд╣рдиреНрддреЗрд░реНрдорд╛рдЩрд┐ тАв рд▓реБрдЩрд┐ рдЪ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рдзрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рд╕ рдЪрд╛рджрдиреНрддрдГ ред рд╕рд┐рдЪ рдЗрдЯреН ред рдЕрддреЛ рд▓реЛрдкрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд┐рд╡рджреНрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН рд╡реГрджреНрдзреНрдпрднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рд░рд┐рд░рд┐рд╖рдГ ред тАШ рд░рд┐рд╖ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдпрд╛рдореН’ ред рдгреНрдпрдиреНрддрд╛рддреН рд▓реБрдЩрд┐ рдЪрдЩрд┐ рдгрд┐рд▓реЛрдкреЛрдкрдзрд╛рд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреАрдирд┐ ред рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдГ рдкрджрдХрд╛рд▓реАрдиреЛрд╜рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInjure not, Rudra, those amongst us who are old or young, who are capable of begetting, or who are begotten, nor a father, nor a mother, nor afflict our precious person ns.тАЭ

Not the great one among us nor the wee little one, not the growing one among us nor the grownтАФ

bodies, Rudra.

Griffith

O Rudra, harm not either great or small of us, harm not the growing boy, harm not the full-grown man.
Slay not a sire among us, slay no mother here, and to our own dear bodies, Rudra, do not harm.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд░реБрджреНрд░рдВ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдорд╛ рдмрдзреАрд░реБрддрд╛рдкрд┐ рдиреЛрд╜рд░реНрднрдХрдВ рдорд╛ рдмрдзреАрдГред рди рдЙрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрдВ рдорд╛ рдмрдзреАрд░реБрддрд╛рдкрд┐ рди рдЙрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдВ рдорд╛ рдмрдзреАрдГред рдирдГ рдкрд┐рддрд░рдВ рдорд╛ рдмрдзреАрдГ рдЙрдд рдорд╛рддрд░рдВ рдорд╛ рдмрдзреАрдГред рдирдГ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрдиреНрд╡рд╕реНрддрдиреВ рдорд╛рдВ рдмрдзреАрд░рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреЛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рд░реАрд░рд┐рд╖рдГ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢рдГ рдХрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддреЗрддреЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН) рд╡рдпреЛрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдВ рдЬрдирдореН (рдЙрдд) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рдорд╛) (рдирдГ) (рдЕрд░реНрднрдХрдореН) рдмрд╛рд▓реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдиреНрдирдореН (рдорд╛) (рдирдГ) (рдЙрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрдореН) рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реЗрдЪрдирд╕рдорд░реНрдердВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдирдореН (рдЙрдд) (рдорд╛) (рдирдГ) (рдЙрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдореН) рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реЗрдЪрдирд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдВ рдЧрд░реНрднрдореН (рдорд╛) (рдирдГ) (рдмрдзреАрдГ) рд╣рд┐рдиреНрдзрд┐ (рдкрд┐рддрд░рдореН) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдВ рдЬрдирдХрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдорд╛) (рдЙрдд) (рдорд╛рддрд░рдореН) рдорд╛рдирд╕рдиреНрдорд╛рдирдХрд░реНрддреНрд░реА рдЬрдирдиреАрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реАрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдорд╛) (рдирдГ) (рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдГ) рдЕрднреАрдкреНрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдГ (рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ) рддрдиреВрдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ (рд░реБрджреНрд░) рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд░реЛрджрдпрд┐рддрдГ (рд░реАрд░рд┐рд╖рдГ) рдЬрд╣рд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рддреБрдЬрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреНрджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHarm us not, Rudra, in our sons or grandsons, or other male descendants, nor in our cattle, nor in our horses; inflamed with anger, kill not our valiant men, for we, presenting clarified butter perpetually invoke you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

DonтАЩt do harm to our progeny and posterity nor to our (own) lifespan, not to our cows nor to our horses.
DonтАЩt smite our heroes, Rudra, when enraged. We, with our oblations, will always invoke you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The bahuvr─лhi ├бriс╣гta-v─лra- тАШpossessing heroes who cannot be harmedтАЩ in 3d is echoed by v─лr─Б╠Бn m─Б тАж vadh─лс╕е тАЬDonтАЩt smite our heroes,тАЭ with the cmpd evoked by r─лriс╣гaс╕е тАШdonтАЩt harmтАЩ, which ends the preceding p─Бda. I suggest that the pattern of p─Бda-init. m─Б╠Бfound through all of vs. 7 and the 1st half of 8 is broken here so that r─лriс╣гah / v─лr─Б╠Бn can be juxtaposed.

The final p─Бda of the vs. also recalls vs. 3, in a somewhat sly way: 3d ends juhav─Бma te hav├нс╕е тАЬWe will pour you an oblation,тАЭ with an etymological figure as noted above. Compare 8d hav├нс╣гmantaс╕е тАж tv─Б hav─Бmahe, also with a form of hav├нsand a 1st pl. verb, which, despite its superficial similarity to juhav─Бma, belongs to the separate root тИЪh┼л, hv─Б тАШcallтАЩ, which has been amply represented in the hymn by the alternative pres. stem hvay─Бmahe (4b, 5b).

The adv. s├бdam тАШalwaysтАЩ is almost always followed by ├нd, which seems to add no special nuance.

Griffith

Harm us not, Rudra, in our seed and progeny, harm us not in the living, nor in cows or steeds,
Slay not our heroes in the fury of thy wrath. Bringing oblations evermore we call to thee.

Geldner

Nicht sollst du uns den leiblichen Samen, nicht an unserem eigenen Leben, nicht an unseren K├╝hen und Pferden sch├дdigen. Nicht sollst du im Grimm unsere Mannen t├╢ten, o Rudra. Mit Opferspenden rufen wir dich immerdar an.

Grassmann

Nicht f├╝ge uns an Kind und Enkeln Schaden zu, an Leuten nicht, an Rindern nicht, an Rossen nicht; O Rudra, t├╢dte unsre Helden nicht im Zorn, Dir Opfer bringend rufen immer wir dich an.

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдХреНрд░реЛрдзрд┐рдд рдЭрд╛рд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрдиреА рдХреБрдгрд╛рдЪреЗрд╣реА рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдиреЗ рд╣рдирди рдХрд░реВ рдирдпреЗ рд╡ рдЧрд╛рдп рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдкрд╢реВрдВрдЪреЗ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрд▓рд╛рд╣реА рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдпрд╛рдиреЗ рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рдЖрдирдВрджреА рд░рд╛рд╣рд┐рд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ рд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдиреА рдорд┐рд│реВрди рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердирд╛ рдХреЗрд▓реА рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ рдХреА рд╣реЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛! рддреБрдЭреНрдпрд╛ рдХреГрдкреЗрдиреЗ рдЖрдореНрд╣реА рдмрд╛рд▓реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдереЗрдд рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╣ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рд╡рд╛рдИрдЯ рдХрд╛рдо рдХрд░реВрди рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рдХрдзреА рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░реВ рдирдпреЗ. рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдВрдиреАрд╣реА рдЖрдордЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░реБрджреНрдз рдХрдзреА рдХрд╛рдо рдХрд░реВ рдирдпреЗ рд╡ рдЬрдЧрд╛рд╡рд░ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛ рдЧрд╛рдп рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдкрд╢реВрдВрдЪрд╛ рдХрдзреА рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░реВ рдирдпреЗ. рее рео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI restore to you the praises (derived from you), as a shepherd (returns his sheep to their owner); father of the Maruts, bestow happiness upon me; your auspicious benignityis the cause of successive delight, therefore we especially solicit your protection.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like a cowherd, I have driven these praises close to you. Grant your favor to us, father of the Maruts,
for your benevolence is auspicious, most merciful. It is just your aid
that we choose.

Griffith

Even as a herdsman I have brought thee hymns of praise: O Father of the Maruts, give us happiness,
Blessed is thy most favouring benevolence, so, verily, do we desire thy saving help.

Geldner

Ich habe dir Loblieder zugetrieben wie der Hirt die Herde heimtreibt. Schenk uns, du Vater der Marut, deine Huld! Denn segensreich ist dein Wohlwollen, sehr barmherzig. Darum bitten wir uns nur deine Gunst aus.

Grassmann

Zu dir hin trieb ich Lieder wie der Hirt das Vieh; O Vater du der Maruts, schenk uns deine Huld; Denn deine Gunst ist heilsam, h├╢chster Gnade voll, drum flehen wir so recht um deinen Schutz dich an.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDestroyer of heroes, may your cow-killing or man-slaying (weapon) be far away, and let the felicity granted by you be ours; favour us; speak, brilliant hero, in our behalf, and grant us, you who are mighty over the two (realms of heaven and earth), prosperity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In the distance be your cow-smiting and men-smiting (anger). You who rule over heroes, let your favor be on us.
Both be merciful to us and speak on our behalf, o god, and then extend double-lofty shelter to us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. supply тАШweaponтАЩ with goghn├бm тАж p┼лruс╣гaghn├бm, and this is certainly possible. I supply тАШangerтАЩ (h├йс╕╖as-) because of the similarity of this clause (─Бr├й te goghn├бm ut├б p┼лruс╣гaghn├бm to 4c ─Бr├й asm├бd da├нvyaс╣Г h├йс╕╖o asyatu.

On neut. dvib├бrh─Бс╕е see comm. ad VII.24.2.

Griffith

Far be thy dart that killeth men or cattle: thy bliss be with us, O thou Lord of Heroes.
Be gracious unto us, O God, and bless us, and then vouchsafe us doubly-strong protection.

Geldner

Fern sei deine Rinder und M├дnner mordende Waffe; du M├дnnerbeherrscher, bei uns soll deine Gnade sein. Erbarme dich unser und sei unser F├╝rsprecher, o Gott, und gew├дhre uns doppelten Schirm!

Grassmann

Lass fern sein, was den Rindern und Menschen verderblich ist; o M├дnnerherrscher, bei uns sei dein Wohlwollen; sei uns gn├дdig und sprich uns freundlich zu, o Gott, und reiche uns nun Schutz, der du zwiefache St├дrke besitzest.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╡реЛ рд╡рдпрдорд╕реНрдореИ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдп рдирдореЛрд╜рд╡реЛрдЪрд╛рдо рд╕ рдорд░реБрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд░реБрджреНрд░реЛ рдирд╕реНрддрдиреНрдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╣рд╡рдВ рдЪ рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреБред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдиреНрдиреЛ рдирдореЛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгреЛрд╜рджрд┐рддрд┐рдГ рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреБрдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдЙрдд рджреНрдпреМрд░реНрд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрднрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рдорд╛рдорд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рдореН рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╡реЛрдЪрд╛рдо) рд╡рджреЗрдо (рдирдордГ) рдирдорд╕реНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ) рдорд╛рдирдиреАрдпрд╛рдп рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдп (рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╡рдГ) рдЖрддреНрдордиреЛрд╜рд╡реЛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд╡рдГ (рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреБ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╣рд╡рдореН) рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░реВрдкрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрдореН (рд░реБрджреНрд░рдГ) рдЕрдзреАрддрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдГ (рдорд░реБрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН (рддрддреН) (рдирдГреж) рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реНрдереИрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реИ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдЪрд░рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬрднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рдЪрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдорд┐рд▓рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдореБрдиреНрдиреАрдпрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдВ рдирд┐рд░рд╛рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрдГ рее резрез реердЕрддреНрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░рд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╕рднрд╛рд╕рджрд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрддреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рдмреЛрдзреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢реЛрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдиреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рд▓рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рд╡рд╛рдЯреЗрд▓ рдЕрд╕реЗ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдирд┐рддреНрдп рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ рд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рдРрдХрд╛рд╡реЗ. рдЕрд╢рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рдорд┐рд│реВрди рдиреНрдпрд╛рдп рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдВрдЧрдд рдХрд░реВрди рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рдп рджреВрд░ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛. рее резрез рее
